alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/15px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:Katrina" title="Template:Katrina">\n             <abbr title="View this template">\n              v\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Katrina" title="Template talk:Katrina">\n             <abbr title="Discuss this template">\n              t\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Katrina&amp;action=edit">\n             <abbr title="Edit this template">\n              e\n             </abbr>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        Hurricane Katrina\n       </b>\n       was an extremely destructive and deadly\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        tropical cyclone\n       </a>\n       that was one of the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_costliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of costliest Atlantic hurricanes">\n        costliest\n       </a>\n       natural disasters and one of the five\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_deadliest_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of deadliest Atlantic hurricanes">\n        deadliest\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">\n        hurricanes\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">\n        history of the United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also was the costliest US disaster until\n       <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2017\n       </a>\n       , when\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Harvey" title="Hurricane Harvey">\n        Hurricane Harvey\n       </a>\n       hit the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Gulf_Coast" title="United States Gulf Coast">\n        United States Gulf Coast\n       </a>\n       . It was the eleventh\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">\n        named storm\n       </a>\n       , the fifth hurricane, and the third major hurricane of the record-breaking\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2005 Atlantic hurricane season\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The storm originated over the Bahamas on August\xc2\xa023 from the interaction between a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">\n        tropical wave\n       </a>\n       and the remnants of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Ten_(2005)" title="Tropical Depression Ten (2005)">\n        Tropical Depression Ten\n       </a>\n       . Early the following day, the new depression intensified into Tropical Storm Katrina. The cyclone headed generally westward toward\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n        Florida\n       </a>\n       and strengthened into a hurricane only two hours before making landfall at\n       <a href="/wiki/Hallandale_Beach,_Florida" title="Hallandale Beach, Florida">\n        Hallandale Beach\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Aventura,_Florida" title="Aventura, Florida">\n        Aventura\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa025. After very briefly weakening to a tropical storm, Katrina emerged into the Gulf of Mexico on August\xc2\xa026 and began to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">\n        rapidly deepen\n       </a>\n       . The storm strengthened to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_5" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">\n        Category 5\n       </a>\n       hurricane over the warm waters of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but weakened before making its second landfall as a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale#Category_3" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">\n        Category 3\n       </a>\n       hurricane on August 29, in southeast Louisiana.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The storm caused severe destruction along the Gulf coast from central Florida to Texas, much of it due to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">\n        storm surge\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">\n        levee\n       </a>\n       failure. Severe property damage occurred in coastal areas, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Effect_of_Hurricane_Katrina_on_Mississippi" title="Effect of Hurricane Katrina on Mississippi">\n        Mississippi beachfront towns\n       </a>\n       where boats and casino barges rammed buildings, pushing cars and houses inland; water reached 6\xe2\x80\x9312 miles (10\xe2\x80\x9319\xc2\xa0km) from the beach. The storm was the third most intense United States landfalling tropical cyclone, behind the\n       <a href="/wiki/1935_Labor_Day_hurricane" title="1935 Labor Day hurricane">\n        1935 Labor Day hurricane\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">\n        Hurricane Camille\n       </a>\n       in 1969. Overall, at least 1,245\xc2\xa0people died in the hurricane and subsequent floods, making it the deadliest United States hurricane since the\n       <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">\n        1928 Okeechobee hurricane\n       </a>\n       . Total property damage was estimated at $108 billion (2005 USD),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       roughly four times the damage wrought by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">\n        Hurricane Andrew\n       </a>\n       in 1992 in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andrewtcr_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-andrewtcr-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over fifty breaches in\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n        New Orleans\n       </a>\n       \'s hurricane surge protection were the cause of the majority of the death and destruction during Katrina on August 29, 2005. Eventually 80% of the city and large tracts of neighboring\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_parishes_of_Louisiana" title="List of parishes of Louisiana">\n        parishes\n       </a>\n       became flooded, and the floodwaters lingered for weeks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to a modeling exercise conducted by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="U.S. Army Corps of Engineers">\n        U.S. Army Corps of Engineers\n       </a>\n       (USACE), two-thirds of the deaths in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_New_Orleans" title="Greater New Orleans">\n        Greater New Orleans\n       </a>\n       were due to levee and floodwall failure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All of the major studies concluded that the USACE, the designers and builders of the levee system as mandated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">\n        Flood Control Act of 1965\n       </a>\n       , was responsible. This is mainly due to a decision to use shorter steel sheet pilings in an effort to save money.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In January 2008, Judge\n       <a href="/wiki/Stanwood_Duval" title="Stanwood Duval">\n        Stanwood Duval\n       </a>\n       , U.S. District Court, ruled that despite the Corps\' role in the flooding, the agency\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       could not be held financially liable because of\n       <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_immunity" title="Sovereign immunity">\n        sovereign immunity\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1928" title="Flood Control Act of 1928">\n        Flood Control Act of 1928\n       </a>\n       . Exactly ten years after Katrina, J. David Rogers, lead author of a new report in the official journal of the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Water_Council" title="World Water Council">\n        World Water Council\n       </a>\n       concluded that the flooding during Katrina "could have been prevented had the corps retained an external review board to double-check its flood-wall designs."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There was also an investigation of the responses from federal, state and local governments, resulting in the resignation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">\n        Federal Emergency Management Agency\n       </a>\n       (FEMA) director\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Brown" title="Michael D. Brown">\n        Michael D. Brown\n       </a>\n       , and of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans_Police_Department" title="New Orleans Police Department">\n        New Orleans Police Department\n       </a>\n       (NOPD) Superintendent\n       <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Compass" title="Eddie Compass">\n        Eddie Compass\n       </a>\n       . Many other government officials were criticized for their responses, especially New Orleans Mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Ray_Nagin" title="Ray Nagin">\n        Ray Nagin\n       </a>\n       , Louisiana Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Blanco" title="Kathleen Blanco">\n        Kathleen Blanco\n       </a>\n       , and President\n       <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n        George W. Bush\n       </a>\n       . Several agencies including the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">\n        United States Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       (USCG),\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">\n        National Hurricane Center\n       </a>\n       (NHC), and\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">\n        National Weather Service\n       </a>\n       (NWS) were commended for their actions. The NHC provided accurate hurricane forecasts with sufficient lead time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CongressInvestigation_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CongressInvestigation-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n      Louisiana\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-10">\n             <a href="#New_Orleans">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">\n        Meteorological history\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Meteorological_history_of_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Meteorological history of Hurricane Katrina">\n        Meteorological history of Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2005_track.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Katrina_2005_track.png/220px-Katrina_2005_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Katrina_2005_track.png/330px-Katrina_2005_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Katrina_2005_track.png/440px-Katrina_2005_track.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2005_track.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm, according to the\n         <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale">\n          Saffir\xe2\x80\x93Simpson scale\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Hurricane Katrina formed as Tropical Depression Twelve over the southeastern Bahamas on August 23, 2005, as the result of an interaction between a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">\n        tropical wave\n       </a>\n       and the remnants of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Ten_(2005)" title="Tropical Depression Ten (2005)">\n        Tropical Depression Ten\n       </a>\n       . The storm strengthened into\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_low" title="Tropical low">\n        Tropical Storm\n       </a>\n       Katrina on the morning of August 24. The tropical storm moved towards Florida, and became a hurricane only two hours before making\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">\n        landfall\n       </a>\n       between\n       <a href="/wiki/Hallandale_Beach,_Florida" title="Hallandale Beach, Florida">\n        Hallandale Beach\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Aventura,_Florida" title="Aventura, Florida">\n        Aventura\n       </a>\n       on the morning of August 25. The storm weakened over land, but it regained hurricane status about one hour after entering the Gulf of Mexico, and it continued strengthening over open waters. On August 27, the storm reached Category 3 intensity on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale">\n        Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale\n       </a>\n       , becoming the third\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_scales#Atlantic_and_East_Pacific" title="Tropical cyclone scales">\n        major hurricane\n       </a>\n       of the season. An\n       <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">\n        eyewall replacement cycle\n       </a>\n       disrupted the intensification, but caused the storm to nearly double in size.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">\n        rapidly intensified\n       </a>\n       after entering the Gulf, growing from a Category 3 hurricane to a Category 5 hurricane in just nine hours. This rapid growth was due to the storm\'s movement over the "unusually warm"\n       <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">\n        waters\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Loop_Current" title="Loop Current">\n        Loop Current\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg/220px-NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg/330px-NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg/440px-NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NOAA-Hurricane-Katrina-Aug28-05-2145UTC.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Katrina on August 28, nearing the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" title="Gulf Coast">\n          Gulf Coast\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Katrina attained Category 5 status on the morning of August 28 and reached its peak strength at 1800\n       <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">\n        UTC\n       </a>\n       that day, with maximum sustained winds of 175\xc2\xa0mph (280\xc2\xa0km/h) and a minimum central\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">\n        pressure\n       </a>\n       of 902\n       <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">\n        mbar\n       </a>\n       (26.6\n       <a href="/wiki/Inch_of_mercury" title="Inch of mercury">\n        inHg\n       </a>\n       ). The pressure measurement made Katrina the fourth most intense Atlantic hurricane on record at the time, only to be surpassed by Hurricanes\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">\n        Rita\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">\n        Wilma\n       </a>\n       later in the season; it was also the strongest hurricane ever recorded in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">\n        Gulf of Mexico\n       </a>\n       at the time. However, this record was later broken by Hurricane Rita.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The hurricane subsequently weakened, and Katrina made its second landfall at 1110 UTC on August 29 as a Category 3 hurricane with sustained winds of 125\xc2\xa0mph (200\xc2\xa0km/h) near\n       <a href="/wiki/Buras-Triumph,_Louisiana" title="Buras-Triumph, Louisiana">\n        Buras-Triumph, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       . At landfall, hurricane-force winds extended outward 120 miles (190\xc2\xa0km) from the center and the storm\'s central pressure was 920\xc2\xa0mbar (27\xc2\xa0inHg). After moving over southeastern Louisiana and\n       <a href="/wiki/Breton_Sound" title="Breton Sound">\n        Breton Sound\n       </a>\n       , it made its third landfall near the Louisiana\xe2\x80\x93Mississippi border with 120\xc2\xa0mph (190\xc2\xa0km/h) sustained winds, still at Category 3 intensity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Katrina maintained strength well into Mississippi, finally losing hurricane strength more than 150 miles (240\xc2\xa0km) inland near\n       <a href="/wiki/Meridian,_Mississippi" title="Meridian, Mississippi">\n        Meridian, Mississippi\n       </a>\n       . It was downgraded to a tropical depression near\n       <a href="/wiki/Clarksville,_Tennessee" title="Clarksville, Tennessee">\n        Clarksville, Tennessee\n       </a>\n       , but its remnants were last distinguishable in the eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       region on August 31, when it was absorbed by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Surface_weather_analysis#Cold_front" title="Surface weather analysis">\n        frontal boundary\n       </a>\n       . The resulting\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extratropical" title="Extratropical">\n        extratropical\n       </a>\n       storm moved rapidly to the northeast and affected eastern Canada.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preparations">\n        Preparations\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Preparations_for_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Preparations for Hurricane Katrina">\n        Preparations for Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_government">\n        Federal government\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BUSHLA.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="515" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/BUSHLA.jpg/220px-BUSHLA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/BUSHLA.jpg/330px-BUSHLA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/BUSHLA.jpg/440px-BUSHLA.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BUSHLA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flanked by\n         <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chertoff" title="Michael Chertoff">\n          Michael Chertoff\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Homeland_Security" title="Secretary of Homeland Security">\n          Secretary of Homeland Security\n         </a>\n         , left, and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Defense" title="Secretary of Defense">\n          Secretary of Defense\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Donald_Rumsfeld" title="Donald Rumsfeld">\n          Donald Rumsfeld\n         </a>\n         , President\n         <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n          George W. Bush\n         </a>\n         meets with members of the\n         <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">\n          White House\n         </a>\n         Task Force on Hurricane Katrina Recovery on August 31, 2005, in the Cabinet Room of the White House.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">\n        United States Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       began pre-positioning resources in a ring around the expected impact zone and activated more than 400 reservists. On August 27, it moved its personnel out of the New Orleans region prior to the mandatory evacuation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Aircrews from the Aviation Training Center, in Mobile, staged rescue aircraft from Texas to Florida.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CG_leadership_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CG_leadership-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       All aircraft were returning towards the Gulf of Mexico by the afternoon of August 29. Air\n       <a href="/wiki/Crew" title="Crew">\n        crews\n       </a>\n       , many of whom lost their homes during the hurricane, began a round-the-clock rescue effort in New Orleans, and along the Mississippi and Alabama coastlines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP_Coast_Guard_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WP_Coast_Guard-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">\n        President of the United States\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">\n        George W. Bush\n       </a>\n       declared a state of emergency in selected regions of Louisiana, Alabama and Mississippi on August 27.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       "On Sunday, August 28, President Bush spoke with Governor Blanco to encourage her to order a mandatory evacuation of New Orleans."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, during the testimony by former\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">\n        Federal Emergency Management Agency\n       </a>\n       (FEMA) chief\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Brown" title="Michael D. Brown">\n        Michael Brown\n       </a>\n       before a U.S. House subcommittee on September\xc2\xa026, Representative\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Buyer" title="Stephen Buyer">\n        Stephen Buyer\n       </a>\n       (R-IN) inquired as to why President Bush\'s declaration of state of emergency of August 27 had not included the coastal parishes of Orleans, Jefferson, and Plaquemines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown_testimony_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Brown_testimony-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The declaration actually did not include any of Louisiana\'s coastal parishes, whereas the coastal counties were included in the declarations for\n       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">\n        Mississippi\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">\n        Alabama\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Brown testified that this was because Louisiana\n       <a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Blanco" title="Kathleen Blanco">\n        Governor Blanco\n       </a>\n       had not included those parishes in her initial request for aid, a decision that he found "shocking." After the hearing, Blanco released a copy of her letter, which showed she had requested assistance for "all the southeastern parishes including the City of New Orleans" as well specifically naming 14 parishes, including Jefferson, Orleans, St. Bernard and Plaquemines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Voluntary and mandatory evacuations were issued for large areas of southeast Louisiana as well as coastal Mississippi and Alabama. About 1.2 million residents of the Gulf Coast were covered under a voluntary or mandatory evacuation order.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration_(NOAA)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration_.28NOAA.29">\n        National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration (NOAA)\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       On the afternoon of August\xc2\xa026, the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">\n        National Hurricane Center\n       </a>\n       (NHC) realized that Katrina had yet to make the turn toward the Florida Panhandle and ended up revising the predicted track of the storm from the panhandle to the Mississippi coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NHC_disc_014_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NHC_disc_014-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The National Weather Service\'s New Orleans/Baton Rouge office issued a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service_bulletin_for_New_Orleans_region" title="National Weather Service bulletin for New Orleans region">\n        vividly worded bulletin\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa028 predicting that the area would be "uninhabitable for weeks" after "devastating damage" caused by Katrina, which at that time rivaled the intensity of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">\n        Hurricane Camille\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During video conferences involving the president later that day and on August\xc2\xa029, NHC director\n       <a href="/wiki/Max_Mayfield" title="Max Mayfield">\n        Max Mayfield\n       </a>\n       expressed concern that Katrina might push its storm surge over the city\'s levees and flood walls. In one conference, he stated, "I do not think anyone can tell you with confidence right now whether the levees will be topped or not, but that\'s obviously a very, very great concern."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levee_Breach_Warning_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Levee_Breach_Warning-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, the National Hurricane Center issued many\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">\n        tropical cyclone warnings and watches\n       </a>\n       throughout the duration of Katrina:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto;">\n       <caption>\n        Summary of\n        <a      <tr>\n        <td style="background-color:#ff8f20">\n         Hurricane Watch\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_City,_Louisiana" title="Intracoastal City,  </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="5">\n         August\xc2\xa028\n        </td>\n        <td rowspan="4">\n         03:00\xc2\xa0UTC\n        </td>\n        <td style="background-color:#ff6060">\n         Hurricane Warning\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Morgan City, Louisiana, to Florida-Alabama border, including\n         <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">\n          Lake Pontchartrain\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background-color:#ffc140">\n         Tropical Storm Warning\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Florida-Alabama border to\n         <a href="/wiki/Destin,_Florida" title="Destin, Florida">\n          Destin, Florida\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background-color:#ffc140">\n         Tropical Storm Warning\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Intracoastal City to Morgan City, Louisiana\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background-color:#ff8f20">\n         Hurricane Watch\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Florida-Alabama border to Destin, Florida\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         09:00\xc2\xa0UTC\n        </td>\n        <td style="background-color:#ffc140">\n         Tropical Storm Warning\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Destin to\n         <a href="/wiki/Indian_Pass,_Florida" title="Indian Pass, Florida">\n          Indian Pass, Florida\n         </a>\n         , and Intracoastal City to\n         <a href="/wiki/Cameron,_Louisiana" title="Cameron, Louisiana">\n          Cameron, Louisiana\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="3">\n         August\xc2\xa029\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         15:00\xc2\xa0UTC\n        </td>\n        <td style="background-color:#c0c0c0">\n         Hurricane Watches discontinued\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         All\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="2">\n         21:00\xc2\xa0UTC\n        </td>\n        <td style="background-color:#ffc140">\n         Tropical Storm Warning\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Pearl River, Louisiana, to Florida-Alabama border\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="background-color:#c0c0c0">\n         Tropical Storm and Hurricane Warning discontinued\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Cameron to Pearl River, Louisiana, and Florida-Alabama border to Destin, Florida\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         August\xc2\xa030\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         03:00\xc2\xa0UTC\n        </td>\n        <td style="background-color:#c0c0c0">\n         Tropical Storm Warning discontinued\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         All\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Florida_and_Gulf_Coast">\n        Florida and Gulf Coast\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In Florida, Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Jeb_Bush" title="Jeb Bush">\n        Jeb Bush\n       </a>\n       declared a\n       <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">\n        state of emergency\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa024 in advance of Hurricane Katrina\'s landfall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida-preps_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Florida-preps-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By the following day, Florida\'s Emergency Operations Center was activated in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tallahassee,_Florida" title="Tallahassee, Florida">\n        Tallahassee\n       </a>\n       to monitor the progress of the hurricane.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before Katrina moved ashore, schools and businesses were closed in the Miami area. Cruise ships altered their paths due to seaports in southeastern Florida closing.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Officials in Miami-Dade County advised residents in mobile homes or with special needs to evacuate. To the north in Broward County, residents east of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Intracoastal_Waterway" title="Intracoastal Waterway">\n        Intracoastal Waterway\n       </a>\n       or in mobile homes were advised to leave their homes. Evacuation orders were issued for offshore islands in\n       <a href="/wiki/Palm_Beach_County,_Florida" title="Palm Beach County, Florida">\n        Palm Beach County\n       </a>\n       , and for residents in mobile homes south of Lantana Road. Additionally, a mandatory evacuation was ordered for vulnerable housing in\n       <a href="/wiki/Martin_County,_Florida" title="Martin County, Florida">\n        Martin County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Florida-preps_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Florida-preps-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Shelters were opened across the region.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Officials closed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">\n        Miami International Airport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afp827_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-afp827-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale_%E2%80%93_Hollywood_International_Airport" title="Fort Lauderdale \xe2\x80\x93 Hollywood International Airport">\n        Fort Lauderdale \xe2\x80\x93 Hollywood International Airport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Key_West_International_Airport" title="Key West International Airport">\n        Key West International Airport\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Keys_Marathon_Airport" title="Florida Keys Marathon Airport">\n        Florida Keys Marathon Airport\n       </a>\n       due to the storm. In Monroe and\n       <a href="/wiki/Collier_County,_Florida" title="Collier County, Florida">\n        Collier\n       </a>\n       counties, schools were closed, and a shelter was opened in\n       <a href="/wiki/Immokalee,_Florida" title="Immokalee, Florida">\n        Immokalee\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyt826_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-nyt826-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="455" data-file-width="772" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif/220px-Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif/330px-Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif/440px-Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Katrina_LA_landfall_radar.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Radar loop of Hurricane Katrina making landfall in Louisiana\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On August 28, Alabama Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Bob_Riley" title="Bob Riley">\n        Bob Riley\n       </a>\n       declared a state of emergency for the approaching Hurricane Katrina. On the same day, he requested President Bush to declare "expedited major disaster declaration" for six counties of south Alabama, which was quickly approved. Three-hundred and fifty national guardsmen were called on duty by August\xc2\xa030.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state of Mississippi activated its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_National_Guard" title="United States National Guard">\n        National Guard\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa026 in preparation for the storm\'s landfall. Additionally, the state government activated its Emergency Operations Center the next day, and local governments began issuing evacuation orders. By 6:00 pm\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone_(North_America)" title="Central Time Zone (North America)">\n        CDT\n       </a>\n       on August 28, 11 counties and cities issued evacuation orders, a number which increased to 41 counties and 61 cities by the following morning. Moreover, 57 emergency shelters were established on coastal communities, with 31 additional shelters available to open if needed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CongressInvestigation_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CongressInvestigation-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By Sunday, August 28, most infrastructure along the Gulf Coast had been shut down, including all freight and\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       rail traffic into the evacuation areas as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Waterford_Nuclear_Generating_Station" title="Waterford Nuclear Generating Station">\n        Waterford Nuclear Generating Station\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana">\n        Louisiana\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_preparedness_for_New_Orleans" title="Hurricane preparedness for New Orleans">\n        Hurricane preparedness for New Orleans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2042" data-file-width="3000" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg/300px-New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg/450px-New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg/600px-New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Elevations.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Vertical cross-section of New Orleans, showing maximum levee height of 23 feet (7\xc2\xa0m). Vertical scale exaggerated.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In Louisiana, the state\'s hurricane evacuation plan calls for local governments in areas along and near the coast to evacuate in three phases, starting with the immediate coast 50 hours before the start of tropical storm force winds. Persons in areas designated Phase II begin evacuating 40 hours before the onset of tropical storm winds and those in Phase III areas (including New Orleans) evacuate 30 hours before the start of such winds.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many private caregiving facilities that relied on bus companies and ambulance services for evacuation were unable to evacuate their charges because they waited too long.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-providermag_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-providermag-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Louisiana\'s Emergency Operations Plan Supplement 1C (Part II, Section II, Paragraph D) calls for use of school and other public buses in evacuations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although buses that later flooded were available to transport those dependent upon public transportation, not enough bus drivers were available to drive them as Governor Blanco did not sign an emergency waiver to allow any licensed driver to transport evacuees on school buses.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By August 26, the possibility of unprecedented cataclysm was already being considered. Many of the computer models had shifted the potential path of Katrina 150 miles (240\xc2\xa0km) westward from the Florida Panhandle, putting the city of New Orleans directly in the center of their track probabilities; the chances of a direct hit were forecast at 17%, with strike probability rising to 29% by August 28.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This scenario was considered a potential catastrophe because some parts of New Orleans and the metro area are below sea level. Since the storm surge produced by the hurricane\'s right-front quadrant (containing the strongest winds) was forecast to be 28 feet (8.5\xc2\xa0m), while the levees offered protection to 23 feet (7.0\xc2\xa0m), emergency management officials in New Orleans feared that the storm surge could go over the tops of levees protecting the city, causing major flooding.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At a news conference at 10 am on August 28, shortly after Katrina was upgraded to a Category 5 storm, New Orleans mayor\n       <a href="/wiki/Ray_Nagin" title="Ray Nagin">\n        Ray Nagin\n       </a>\n       ordered the first-ever\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_evacuation" title="Emergency evacuation">\n        mandatory evacuation\n       </a>\n       of the city, calling Katrina "a storm that most of us have long feared."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city government also established several "refuges of last resort" for citizens who could not leave the city, including the massive\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Superdome" title="Louisiana Superdome">\n        Louisiana Superdome\n       </a>\n       , which sheltered approximately 26,000 people and provided them with food and water for several days as the storm came ashore.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some estimates claimed that 80% of the 1.3 million residents of the greater New Orleans metropolitan area evacuated, leaving behind substantially fewer people than remained in the city during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ivan" title="Hurricane Ivan">\n        Hurricane Ivan\n       </a>\n       evacuation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">\n        Impact\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina_effects_by_region" title="Hurricane Katrina effects by region">\n        Hurricane Katrina effects by region\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0"
