      <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Katrina_(short_film_by_NASA).ogv" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          In Katrina\'s Wake\n         </i>\n         \xe2\x80\x93 short film by\n         <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n          NASA\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:0 1em 0.5em;">\n       <caption>\n        Deaths by state\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">\n          Alabama\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">\n          Florida\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         14\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n          Georgia\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n          Kentucky\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">\n          Louisiana\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         986\xe2\x80\x931,577*\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">\n          Mississippi\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         238\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n          Ohio\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Total\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         1,245\xe2\x80\x931,836\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR_2005AHS_44-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-MWR_2005AHS-44">\n           [44]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHHLouisiana_45-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-DHHLouisiana-45">\n           [45]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Missing\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         10\xe2\x80\x9366\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHHLousiana2_46-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-DHHLousiana2-46">\n           [46]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <small>\n          *Includes out-of-state evacuees\n          <br/>\n          counted by Louisiana\n         </small>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       On August 29, Katrina\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">\n        storm surge\n       </a>\n       caused 53 breaches to various flood protection structures in and around the greater New Orleans area, submerging 80% of the city. A June 2007 report by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">\n        American Society of Civil Engineers\n       </a>\n       indicated that two-thirds of the flooding was caused by the multiple failures of the city\'s floodwalls.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCE_HKERP_report_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ASCE_HKERP_report-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The storm surge also devastated the coasts of Mississippi and Alabama, making Katrina the most destructive and costliest\n       <a href="/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">\n        natural disaster\n       </a>\n       in the history of the United States, and the deadliest hurricane since the 1928 Okeechobee Hurricane. The total damage from Katrina is estimated at $108 billion (2005\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._dollars" title="U.S. dollars">\n        U.S. dollars\n       </a>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katreport_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-katreport-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The death toll from Katrina is uncertain, with reports differing by hundreds. According to the National Hurricane Center, 1,836 fatalities can be attributed to the storm: 1 in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       , 2 each in Alabama,\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n        Georgia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       , 14 in Florida, 238 in Mississippi, and 1,577 in Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MWR_2005AHS_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MWR_2005AHS-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-louisiana1_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-louisiana1-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, 135 people remain categorized as missing in Louisiana,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-louisiana1_49-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-louisiana1-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and many of the deaths are indirect, but it is almost impossible to determine the exact cause of some of the fatalities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 2008 report by the Disaster Medicine and Public Health Preparedness journal indicates that 966\xc2\xa0deaths can be directly attributed to the storm in Louisiana, including out of state evacuees, and another 20 indirectly (such as firearm related deaths and gas poisoning). Due to uncertain causes of death with 454\xc2\xa0evacuees, an upper-bound of 1,440 is noted in the paper.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHHLouisiana_45-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DHHLouisiana-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A follow-up study by the Louisiana Department of Health &amp; Hospitals determined that the storm was directly responsible for 1,170\xc2\xa0fatalities in Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DHHLousiana2_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-DHHLousiana2-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">\n        Federal\n       </a>\n       disaster declarations covered 90,000 square miles (230,000\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of the United States, an area almost as large as the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">\n        United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       . The hurricane left an estimated three million people without electricity. On September 3, 2005,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homeland_Security" title="Homeland Security">\n        Homeland Security\n       </a>\n       Secretary\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Chertoff" title="Michael Chertoff">\n        Michael Chertoff\n       </a>\n       described the aftermath of Hurricane Katrina as "probably the worst catastrophe, or set of catastrophes," in the country\'s history, referring to the hurricane itself plus the flooding of New Orleans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Even in 2010, debris remained in some coastal communities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Florida,_Bahamas,_and_Cuba">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Florida.2C_Bahamas.2C_and_Cuba">\n        Florida, Bahamas, and Cuba\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg/220px-Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg/330px-Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg/440px-Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_damage_to_mobile_home_in_Davie_Florida.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damage to a mobile home in\n         <a href="/wiki/Davie,_Florida" title="Davie, Florida">\n          Davie, Florida\n         </a>\n         following Hurricane Katrina\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Katrina_in_Florida" title="Effects of Hurricane Katrina in Florida">\n        Effects of Hurricane Katrina in Florida\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Hurricane Katrina first made landfall between\n       <a href="/wiki/Hallandale_Beach,_Florida" title="Hallandale Beach, Florida">\n        Hallandale Beach\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Aventura,_Florida" title="Aventura, Florida">\n        Aventura, Florida\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa025. The storm dropped heavy rainfall in portions of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">\n        Miami metropolitan area\n       </a>\n       , with a peak total of 16.43\xc2\xa0in (417\xc2\xa0mm) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Perrine,_Florida" title="Perrine, Florida">\n        Perrine\n       </a>\n       . As a result, local flooding occurred in\n       <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">\n        Miami-Dade County\n       </a>\n       , damaging approximately 100\xc2\xa0homes. Farther south in the Florida Keys, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">\n        tornado\n       </a>\n       was spawned in\n       <a href="/wiki/Marathon,_Florida" title="Marathon, Florida">\n        Marathon\n       </a>\n       on August\xc2\xa026. The tornado damaged a hangar at the airport there and caused an estimated $5 million in damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marathon_Tornado_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Marathon_Tornado-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The rains caused flooding, and the combination of rains and winds downed trees and power lines, leaving 1.45\xc2\xa0million people without power. Damage in South Florida was estimated at $523 million, mostly as a result of crop damage. Twelve deaths occurred in South Florida, of which three were caused by downed trees in Broward County, three from drowning in Miami-Dade County, three were from carbon monoxide poisoning caused by generators, one was due to a vehicle accident, one occurred during debris cleanup, and one was associated with a lack of electricity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Significant impact was also reported in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">\n        Florida Panhandle\n       </a>\n       . Although Katrina moved ashore in Louisiana and Mississippi, its outer periphery produced a 5.37\xc2\xa0ft (1.64\xc2\xa0m) storm surge in\n       <a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">\n        Pensacola\n       </a>\n       . High waves caused beach erosion and closed nearby roadways. There were five tornadoes in the northwestern portion of the state, though none of them caused significant damage. Throughout the Florida Panhandle, the storm resulted in an estimated $100\xc2\xa0million in damage. There were two indirect fatalities from Katrina in\n       <a href="/wiki/Walton_County,_Florida" title="Walton County, Florida">\n        Walton County\n       </a>\n       as a result of a traffic accident.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the Florida Panhandle, 77,000\xc2\xa0customers lost power.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall, the hurricane killed 14\xc2\xa0people and caused at least $623\xc2\xa0million in damage.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Before striking South Florida, Katrina traversed the Bahamas as a tropical storm. However, minimal impact was reported, with only "fresh breezes" on various islands.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wmo_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-wmo-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although Hurricane Katrina stayed well to the north of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">\n        Cuba\n       </a>\n       , on August 29 it brought tropical-storm force winds and rainfall of over 8\xc2\xa0in (200\xc2\xa0mm) to western regions of the island. Telephone and power lines were damaged and around 8,000\xc2\xa0people were evacuated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pinar_del_R%C3%ADo_Province" title="Pinar del R\xc3\xado Province">\n        Pinar del R\xc3\xado Province\n       </a>\n       . According to Cuban television reports the coastal town of Surgidero de Bataban\xc3\xb3 was 90% underwater.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cuba_damage_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Cuba_damage-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Louisiana_2">\n        Louisiana\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PostVeniceLG.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/PostVeniceLG.jpg/220px-PostVeniceLG.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/PostVeniceLG.jpg/330px-PostVeniceLG.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/PostVeniceLG.jpg/440px-PostVeniceLG.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PostVeniceLG.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flooding in\n         <a href="/wiki/Venice,_Louisiana" title="Venice, Louisiana">\n          Venice, Louisiana\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On August 29, Hurricane Katrina made landfall near\n       <a href="/wiki/Buras-Triumph,_Louisiana" title="Buras-Triumph, Louisiana">\n        Buras-Triumph, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , with 125\xc2\xa0mph (200\xc2\xa0km/h) winds, a strong Category 3 storm. However, as it had only just weakened from Category 4 strength and the radius of maximum winds was large, it is possible that sustained winds of Category 4 strength briefly impacted extreme southeastern Louisiana. Although the storm surge to the east of the path of the eye in Mississippi was higher, a very significant surge affected the Louisiana coast. The height of the surge is uncertain because of a lack of data, although a tide gauge in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaquemines_Parish" title="Plaquemines Parish">\n        Plaquemines Parish\n       </a>\n       indicated a storm tide in excess of 14 feet (4.3\xc2\xa0m) and a 12-foot (3.7\xc2\xa0m) storm surge was recorded in\n       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Isle,_Louisiana" title="Grand Isle, Louisiana">\n        Grand Isle\n       </a>\n       . Hurricane Katrina made final landfall near the mouth of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_(Mississippi%E2%80%93Louisiana)" title="Pearl River (Mississippi\xe2\x80\x93Louisiana)">\n        Pearl River\n       </a>\n       , with the eye straddling\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Tammany_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Tammany Parish, Louisiana">\n        St. Tammany Parish, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County,_Mississippi" title="Hancock County, Mississippi">\n        Hancock County, Mississippi\n       </a>\n       , on the morning of August 29 at about 9:45M CST.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hurricane Katrina also brought heavy rain to Louisiana, with 8\xe2\x80\x9310 inches (200\xe2\x80\x93250\xc2\xa0mm) falling on a wide swath of the eastern part of the state. In the area around\n       <a href="/wiki/Slidell,_Louisiana" title="Slidell, Louisiana">\n        Slidell\n       </a>\n       , the rainfall was even higher, and the highest rainfall recorded in the state was approximately 15 inches (380\xc2\xa0mm). As a result of the rainfall and storm surge the level of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain" title="Lake Pontchartrain">\n        Lake Pontchartrain\n       </a>\n       rose and caused significant flooding along its northeastern shore, affecting communities from Slidell to\n       <a href="/wiki/Mandeville,_Louisiana" title="Mandeville, Louisiana">\n        Mandeville\n       </a>\n       . Several bridges were destroyed, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/I-10_Twin_Span_Bridge" title="I-10 Twin Span Bridge">\n        I-10 Twin Span Bridge\n       </a>\n       connecting Slidell to New Orleans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Almost 900,000 people in Louisiana lost power as a result of Hurricane Katrina.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Power_failures_56-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Power_failures-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Katrina\'s storm surge inundated all parishes surrounding Lake Pontchartrain, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Tammany" title="St. Tammany">\n        St. Tammany\n       </a>\n       , Tangipahoa,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._John_the_Baptist" title="St. John the Baptist">\n        St. John the Baptist\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Charles_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Charles Parish, Louisiana">\n        St. Charles\n       </a>\n       Parishes. St. Tammany Parish received a two-part storm surge. The first surge came as Lake Pontchartrain rose and the storm blew water from the Gulf of Mexico into the lake. The second came as the eye of Katrina passed, westerly winds pushed water into a bottleneck at the Rigolets Pass, forcing it farther inland. The range of surge levels in eastern St. Tammany Parish is estimated at 13\xe2\x80\x9316 feet (4.0\xe2\x80\x934.9\xc2\xa0m), not including wave action.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Hard-hit\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Parish" title="St. Bernard Parish">\n        St. Bernard Parish\n       </a>\n       was flooded because of breaching of the levees that contained a navigation channel called the Mississippi River Gulf Outlet (MR-GO) and the breach of the 40 Arpent canal levee that was designed and built by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orleans_Levee_Board" title="Orleans Levee Board">\n        Orleans Levee Board\n       </a>\n       . The search for the missing was undertaken by the St. Bernard Fire Department because of the assets of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">\n        United States Coast Guard\n       </a>\n       being diverted to New Orleans. In the months after the storm, many of the missing were tracked down by searching flooded homes, tracking credit card records, and visiting homes of family and relatives.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2086" data-file-width="2062" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/170px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/255px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg/340px-Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2nd_landfall.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Hurricane Katrina making landfall in\n         <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n          New Orleans, Louisiana\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       According to the U.S. Dept. of Housing and Urban Development, in St. Bernard Parish, 81% (20,229) of the housing units were damaged. In St. Tammany Parish, 70% (48,792) were damaged and in Placquemines Parish 80% (7,212) were damaged.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition, the combined effect of Hurricanes Katrina and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Rita" title="Hurricane Rita">\n        Rita\n       </a>\n       was the destruction of an estimated 562 square kilometres (217\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi) of coastal wetlands in Louisiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_Orleans">\n        New Orleans\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Katrina_in_New_Orleans" title="Effects of Hurricane Katrina in New Orleans">\n        Effects of Hurricane Katrina in New Orleans\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_levee_failures_in_Greater_New_Orleans" title="2005 levee failures in Greater New Orleans">\n        2005 levee failures in Greater New Orleans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1514" data-file-width="1153" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg/170px-KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg/255px-KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg/340px-KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KatrinaNewOrleansFlooded_edit2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flooded I-10/I-610/West End Blvd\n         <a href="/wiki/Interchange_(road)" title="Interchange (road)">\n          interchange\n         </a>\n         and surrounding area of northwest New Orleans and Metairie, Louisiana\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       As the eye of Hurricane Katrina swept to the northeast, it subjected the city to hurricane conditions for hours. Although power failures prevented accurate measurement of wind speeds in New Orleans, there were a few measurements of hurricane-force winds. From this the NHC concluded that it is likely that much of the city experienced sustained winds of Category 1 or Category 2 strength.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Katrina\'s storm surge led to 53 levee breaches in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">\n        federally built levee system\n       </a>\n       protecting metro New Orleans and the failure of the 40 Arpent Canal levee. Nearly every levee in metro New Orleans was breached as Hurricane Katrina passed just east of the city limits. Failures occurred in New Orleans and surrounding communities, especially St. Bernard Parish. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_River_Gulf_Outlet" title="Mississippi River Gulf Outlet">\n        Mississippi River Gulf Outlet\n       </a>\n       (MR-GO) breached its levees in approximately 20 places, flooding much of east New Orleans, most of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Bernard_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Saint Bernard Parish, Louisiana">\n        St. Bernard Parish\n       </a>\n       and the East Bank of\n       <a href="/wiki/Plaquemines_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Plaquemines Parish, Louisiana">\n        Plaquemines Parish\n       </a>\n       . The major levee breaches in the city included breaches at the\n       <a href="/wiki/17th_Street_Canal" title="17th Street Canal">\n        17th Street Canal\n       </a>\n       levee, the\n       <a href="/wiki/London_Avenue_Canal" title="London Avenue Canal">\n        London Avenue Canal\n       </a>\n       , and the wide, navigable\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Canal" title="Industrial Canal">\n        Industrial Canal\n       </a>\n       , which left approximately 80% of the city flooded.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most of the major roads traveling into and out of the city were damaged. The only routes out of the city were the westbound\n       <a href="/wiki/Crescent_City_Connection" title="Crescent City Connection">\n        Crescent City Connection\n       </a>\n       and the Huey P. Long Bridge, as large portions of the I-10 Twin Span Bridge traveling eastbound towards Slidell, Louisiana had collapsed. Both the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Pontchartrain_Causeway" title="Lake Pontchartrain Causeway">\n        Lake Pontchartrain Causeway\n       </a>\n       and the Crescent City Connection only carried emergency traffic.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On August 29, at 7:40 am CDT, it was reported that most of the windows on the north side of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hyatt_Regency_New_Orleans" title="Hyatt Regency New Orleans">\n        Hyatt Regency New Orleans\n       </a>\n       had been blown out, and many other high rise buildings had extensive window damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hyatt" title="Hyatt">\n        Hyatt\n       </a>\n       was the most severely damaged hotel in the city, with beds reported to be flying out of the windows. Insulation tubes were exposed as the hotel\'s glass exterior was completely sheared off.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Superdome, which was sheltering many people who had not evacuated, sustained significant damage.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gibson_65-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gibson-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Two sections of the Superdome\'s roof were compromised and the dome\'s waterproof membrane had essentially been peeled off.\n       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armstrong_New_Orleans_International_Airport" title="Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport">\n        Louis Armstrong New Orleans International Airport\n       </a>\n       was closed before the storm but did not flood. On August 30, it was reopened to humanitarian and rescue operations. Limited commercial passenger service resumed at the airport on September 13 and regular carrier operations resumed in early October.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Orleans_Airport_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-New_Orleans_Airport-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Levee breaches in New Orleans also caused a significant number of deaths, with over 700 bodies recovered in New Orleans by October 23, 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some survivors and evacuees reported seeing dead bodies lying in city streets and floating in still-flooded sections, especially in the east of the city. The advanced state of decomposition of many corpses, some of which were left in the water or sun for days before being collected, hindered efforts by coroners to identify many of the dead.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1629" data-file-width="2500" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg/220px-New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg/330px-New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg/440px-New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_Survivor_Flyover.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A U.S. Coast Guardsman searches for survivors in New Orleans in the Katrina aftermath.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first deaths reported from the city were reported shortly before midnight on August 28, as three\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nursing_home" title="Nursing home">\n        nursing home\n       </a>\n       patients died during an evacuation to\n       <a href="/wiki/Baton_Rouge,_Louisiana" title="Baton Rouge, Louisiana">\n        Baton Rouge\n       </a>\n       , most likely from dehydration. An estimated 215 bodies were found in nursing homes and hospitals in New Orleans,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USA20051017_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-USA20051017-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the largest number being at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Medical_Center_and_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Memorial Medical Center and Hurricane Katrina">\n        Memorial Medical Center\n       </a>\n       where 45 corpses were recovered.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some 200 patients at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Charity_Hospital_(New_Orleans)" title="Charity Hospital (New Orleans)">\n        Charity Hospital\n       </a>\n       weren\'t evacuated until Friday September 2, having been without power or fresh water for five days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While there were also early reports of fatalities amid mayhem at the Superdome, only six deaths were confirmed there, with four of these originating from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_causes" title="Natural causes">\n        natural causes\n       </a>\n       , one from a\n       <a href="/wiki/Drug_overdose" title="Drug overdose">\n        drug overdose\n       </a>\n       , and one a\n       <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">\n        suicide\n       </a>\n       . At the Convention Center, four bodies were recovered. One of the four is believed to be the result of a homicide.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thevenot_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-thevenot-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There is evidence that many prisoners were abandoned in their cells during the storm, while the guards sought shelter. Hundreds of prisoners were later registered as "unaccounted for".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mississippi">\n        Mississippi\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_Hurricane_Katrina_in_Mississippi" title="Effects of Hurricane Katrina in Mississippi">\n        Effects of Hurricane Katrina in Mississippi\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="343" data-file-width="515" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg/220px-Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg/330px-Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg/440px-Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Structural_Bridge_Damage.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_90" title="U.S. Route 90">\n          U.S. Route 90\n         </a>\n         \'s Bay St. Louis Bridge on Pass Christian was destroyed as a result of Katrina.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Gulf coast of Mississippi suffered massive damage from the impact of Hurricane Katrina on August 29, leaving 238 people dead, 67 missing, and billions of dollars in damage: bridges, barges, boats, piers, houses and cars were washed inland.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBrecov_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HBrecov-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Katrina traveled up the entire state, and afterwards, all 82 counties in Mississippi were declared disaster areas for federal assistance, 47 for full assistance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HBrecov_77-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-HBrecov-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After making a brief initial landfall in Louisiana, Katrina had made its final landfall near the state line, and the eyewall passed over the cities of Bay St. Louis and Waveland as a Category 3 hurricane with sustained winds of 120\xc2\xa0mph (190\xc2\xa0km/h).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Katrina\'s powerful right-front quadrant passed over the west and central Mississippi coast, causing a powerful 27-foot (8.2\xc2\xa0m) storm surge, which penetrated 6 miles (10\xc2\xa0km) inland in many areas and up to 12 miles (19\xc2\xa0km) inland along bays and rivers; in some areas, the surge crossed\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">\n        Interstate 10\n       </a>\n       for several miles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Hurricane Katrina brought strong winds to Mississippi, which caused significant tree damage throughout the state. The highest unofficial reported wind gust recorded from Katrina was one of 135\xc2\xa0mph (217\xc2\xa0km/h) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Poplarville,_Mississippi" title="Poplarville, Mississippi">\n        Poplarville\n       </a>\n       , in\n       <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_County,_Mississippi" title="Pearl River County, Mississippi">\n        Pearl River County\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg/220px-Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg/330px-Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg/440px-Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_katrina_damage_gulfport_mississippi.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Damage to\n         <a href="/wiki/Long_Beach,_Mississippi" title="Long Beach, Mississippi">\n          Long Beach, Mississippi\n         </a>\n         following Hurricane Katrina\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The storm also brought heavy rains with 8\xe2\x80\x9310 inches (200\xe2\x80\x93250\xc2\xa0mm) falling in southwestern Mississippi and rain in excess of 4 inches (100\xc2\xa0mm) falling throughout the majority of the state. Katrina caused eleven tornadoes in Mississippi on August 29, some of which damaged trees and power lines.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Battered by wind, rain and storm surge, some beachfront neighborhoods were completely leveled. Preliminary estimates by Mississippi officials calculated that 90% of the structures within half a mile of the coastline were completely destroyed,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_Miss_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CBS_Miss-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and that storm surges traveled as much as 6 miles (10\xc2\xa0km) inland in portions of the state\'s coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katreport_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-katreport-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One apartment complex with approximately thirty residents seeking shelter inside collapsed. More than half of the 13 casinos in the state, which were floated on barges to comply with Mississippi land-based gambling laws, were washed hundreds of yards inland by waves.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_Miss_78-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CBS_Miss-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of streets and bridges were washed away. On\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Highway_90" title="U.S. Highway 90">\n        U.S. Highway 90\n       </a>\n       along the Mississippi Gulf Coast, two major bridges were completely destroyed: the Bay St. Louis\xe2\x80\x93Pass Christian\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       bridge, and the Biloxi\xe2\x80\x93\n       <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Springs,_Mississippi" title="Ocean Springs, Mississippi">\n        Ocean Springs\n       </a>\n       bridge. In addition, the eastbound\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Span_(architecture)" title="Span (architecture)">\n        span\n       </a>\n       of the I-10 bridge over the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pascagoula_River" title="Pascagoula River">\n        Pascagoula River\n       </a>\n       estuary was damaged. In the weeks after the storm, with the connectivity of the coastal U.S. Highway 90 shattered, traffic traveling parallel to the coast was reduced first to State Road 11 (parallel to I-10) then to two lanes on the remaining I-10 span when it was opened.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg/220px-Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg/330px-Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg/440px-Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pascagoula_destroyed_condos_from_Katrina.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Surge damage in\n         <a href="/wiki/Pascagoula,_Mississippi" title="Pascagoula, Mississippi">\n          Pascagoula, Mississippi\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       All three coastal counties of the state were severely affected by the storm. Katrina\'s surge was the most extensive, as well as the highest, in the documented history of the United States; large portions of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County,_Mississippi" title="Hancock County, Mississippi">\n        Hancock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrison_County,_Mississippi" title="Harrison County, Mississippi">\n        Harrison\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_County,_Mississippi" title="Jackson County, Mississippi">\n        Jackson\n       </a>\n       counties were inundated by the storm surge, in all three cases affecting most of the populated areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">\n        <a href="#cite_note-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Surge covered almost the entire lower half of Hancock County, destroying the coastal communities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Clermont_Harbor,_Mississippi" title="Clermont Harbor, Mississippi">\n        Clermont Harbor\n       </a>\n       and Waveland, much of Bay St. Louis, and flowed up the Jourdan River, flooding Diamondhead and\n       <a href="/wiki/Kiln,_Mississippi" title="Kiln, Mississippi">\n        Kiln\n       </a>\n       . In Harrison County,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pass_Christian" title="Pass Christian">\n        Pass Christian\n       </a>\n       was completely inundated, along with a narrow strip of land to the east along the coast, which includes the cities of Long Beach and Gulfport; the flooding was more extensive in communities such as D\'Iberville, which borders Back Bay.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biloxi" title="Biloxi">\n        Biloxi\n       </a>\n       , on a peninsula between the Back Bay and the coast, was particularly hard hit, especially the low-lying Point Cadet area. In Jackson County, storm surge flowed up the wide river\n       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">\n        estuary\n       </a>\n       , with the combined surge and freshwater flooding cutting the county in half. Remarkably, over 90% of Pascagoula, the easternmost coastal city in Mississippi, and about 75 miles (120\xc2\xa0km) east of Katrina\'s landfall near the Louisiana-Mississippi border, was flooded from surge at the height of the storm. Other large Jackson County neighborhoods such as Porteaux Bay and Gulf Hills were severely damaged with large portions being completely destroyed, and\n       <a href="/wiki/St._Martin,_Mississippi" title="St. Martin, Mississippi">\n        St. Martin\n       </a>\n       was hard hit; Ocean Springs,\n       <a href="/wiki/Moss_Point,_Mississippi" title="Moss Point, Mississippi">\n        Moss Point\n       </a>\n       , Gautier and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Escatawpa" title="Escatawpa">\n        Escatawpa\n       </a>\n       also suffered major surge damage.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mississippi Emergency Management Agency officials also recorded deaths in\n       <a href="/wiki/Forrest_County,_Mississippi" title="Forrest County, Mississippi">\n        Forrest\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hinds_County,_Mississippi" title="Hinds County, Mississippi">\n        Hinds\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Warren_County,_Mississippi" title="Warren County, Mississippi">\n        Warren\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Leake_County,_Mississippi" title="Leake County, Mississippi">\n        Leake\n       </a>\n       counties. Over 900,000 people throughout the state experienced power outages.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Power_failures_56-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Power_failures-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_United_States">\n        Southeast United States\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="331" data-file-width="500" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg/220px-KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg/330px-KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg/440px-KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KatrinaMobileCourthouseSteps.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Flood waters come up the steps of\n         <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">\n          Mobile\n         </a>\n         \'s federal courthouse.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Although Hurricane Katrina made landfall well to the west, Alabama and the Florida Panhandle were both affected by tropical-storm force winds and a storm surge varying from 12\xc2\xa0to 16 feet (3.7\xe2\x80\x934.9\xc2\xa0m) around\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Bay" title="Mobile Bay">\n        Mobile Bay\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with higher waves on top. Sustained winds of 67\xc2\xa0mph (108\xc2\xa0km/h) were recorded in\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">\n        Mobile, Alabama\n       </a>\n       , and the storm surge there was approximately 12 feet (3.7\xc2\xa0m).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The surge caused significant flooding several miles inland along Mobile Bay. Four tornadoes were also reported in Alabama.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ships, oil rigs, boats and fishing\n       <a href="/wiki/Pier" title="Pier">\n        piers\n       </a>\n       were washed ashore along Mobile Bay: the cargo ship M/V\n       <i>\n        Caribbean Clipper\n       </i>\n       and many fishing boats were grounded at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayou_La_Batre" title="Bayou La Batre">\n        Bayou La Batre\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       An\n       <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">\n        oil rig\n       </a>\n       under construction along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_River" title="Mobile River">\n        Mobile River\n       </a>\n       broke its moorings and floated 1.5 miles (2.4\xc2\xa0km) northwards before striking the Cochrane Bridge just outside Mobile. No significant damage resulted to the bridge and it was soon reopened. The damage on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dauphin_Island" title="Dauphin Island">\n        Dauphin Island\n       </a>\n       was severe, with the surge destroying many houses and cutting a new canal through the western portion of the island. An offshore oil rig also became grounded on the island. As in Mississippi, the storm surge caused significant beach erosion along the Alabama coastline.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KatrinaTCR_1-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KatrinaTCR-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       More than 600,000 people lost power in Alabama as a result of Hurricane Katrina and two people died in a traffic accident in the state. Residents in some areas, such as Selma, were without power for several days.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Power_failures_56-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Power_failures-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="950" data-file-width="1650" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg/220px-Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg/330px-Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg/440px-Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_Bayou_La_Batre_2005_boats_ashore.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bayou_La_Batre" title="Bayou La Batre">\n          Bayou La Batre\n         </a>\n         : cargo ship and fishing boats were grounded\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Northern and central\n       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">\n        Georgia\n       </a>\n       were affected by heavy rains and strong winds from Hurricane Katrina as the storm moved inland, with more than 3 inches (75\xc2\xa0mm) of rain falling in several areas. At least 18 tornadoes formed in Georgia on August 29, the most on record in that state for one day in August. The most serious of these tornadoes was an F2 tornado which affected\n       <a href="/wiki/Heard_County,_Georgia" title="Heard County, Georgia">\n        Heard County\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Carroll_County,_Georgia" title="Carroll County, Georgia">\n        Carroll County\n       </a>\n       . This tornado caused three injuries and one fatality and damaged several houses. The other tornadoes caused significant damages to buildings and agricultural facilities. In addition to the fatality caused by the F2 tornado, there was another fatality in a traffic accident.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Eastern\n       <a href="/wiki/Arkansas" title="Arkansas">\n        Arkansas\n       </a>\n       received light rain from the passage of Katrina.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rain_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-rain-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Gusty winds downed some trees and power lines, though damage was minimal. Katrina also caused a number of power outages in many areas, with over 100,000 customers affected in\n       <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">\n        Tennessee\n       </a>\n       , primarily in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">\n        Memphis\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">\n        Nashville\n       </a>\n       areas.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_U.S._states_and_Canada">\n        Other U.S. states and Canada\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png"        <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          This section\n          <b>\n           needs additional citations for\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">\n            verification\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please help\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Katrina&amp;action=edit">\n            improve this article\n           </a>\n           by\n           <a     . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (August 2017)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="694" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif/220px-Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif/330px-Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif/440px-Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Katrina_2005_rainfall.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Total rainfall from Katrina in the United States. Data for the\n         <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">\n          New Orleans\n         </a>\n         area is not available.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       , a storm that had moved through the weekend before had already produced flooding and the rainfall from Katrina added to this. A 10-year-old girl drowned in\n       <a href="/wiki/Hopkinsville,_Kentucky" title="Hopkinsville, Kentucky">\n        Hopkinsville\n       </a>\n       . Dozens of business were closed and several families evacuated due to rising flood waters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As a result of the flooding,\n       <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Kentucky" title="Governor of Kentucky">\n        Kentucky Governor\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Fletcher" title="Ernie Fletcher">\n        Ernie Fletcher\n       </a>\n       declared three counties disaster areas and a statewide state of emergency.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, wind gusts up to 72\xc2\xa0mph (116\xc2\xa0km/h) resulted in some damage. Downed trees and power lines were reported in several counties in western Kentucky, especially\n       <a href="/wiki/Calloway_County,_Kentucky" title="Calloway County, Kentucky">\n        Calloway\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Christian_County,_Kentucky" title="Christian County, Kentucky">\n        Christian\n       </a>\n       counties. Overall, more than 10,000\xc2\xa0utility customers in western Kentucky experienced power outages. The remnants of Katrina spawned a tornado in Virginia, damaging at least 13\xc2\xa0homes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall,_Virginia" title="Marshall, Virginia">\n        Marshall\n       </a>\n       . In addition, approximately 4,000\xc2\xa0people lost electricity. Over 3\xc2\xa0in (76\xc2\xa0mm) of rain fell in portions of West Virginia, causing localized flooding in several counties. At least 103\xc2\xa0homes and 7\xc2\xa0buildings suffered some degree of water damage. A number of roads and bridges were inundated or washed out. The remnants of Katrina produced locally heavy precipitation in northeast Ohio, ranging from about 2 to 4\xc2\xa0in (51 to 102\xc2\xa0mm). Numerous streams and rivers overflowed their banks, forcing the closure of several roads, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_90_in_Ohio" title="Interstate 90 in Ohio">\n        Interstate 90\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">\n        Cleveland\n       </a>\n       . Two deaths occurred due to a flood-related automobile accident in\n       <a href="/wiki/Huron_County,_Ohio" title="Huron County, Ohio">\n        Huron County\n       </a>\n       . Additionally, hundreds of homes and businesses suffered flood damage.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Katrina spawned five tornadoes in\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       , though none resulted in significant damage. Up to 5\xc2\xa0in (130\xc2\xa0mm) of rain fell in western\n       <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">\n        New York\n       </a>\n       . Gusty winds also left approximately 4,500\xc2\xa0people in\n       <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">\n        Buffalo\n       </a>\n       without electricity. The remnants of Katrina brought 3 to 6\xc2\xa0in (76 to 152\xc2\xa0mm) of rain to portions of Massachusetts, causing flash flooding in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bristol_County,_Massachusetts" title="Bristol County, Massachusetts">\n        Bristol\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_County,_Massachusetts" title="Plymouth County, Massachusetts">\n        Plymouth\n       </a>\n       counties. Several roads were closed due to floodwater inundation in\n       <a href="/wiki/Acushnet,_Massachusetts" title="Acushnet, Massachusetts">\n        Acushnet\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth,_Massachusetts" title="Dartmouth, Massachusetts">\n        Dartmouth\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Bedford,_Massachusetts" title="New Bedford, Massachusetts">\n        New Bedford\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Wareham,_Massachusetts" title="Wareham, Massachusetts">\n        Wareham\n       </a>\n       , including\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Route_18" title="Massachusetts Route 18">\n        Route 18\n       </a>\n       in New Bedford. Very minimal impact was reported in\n       <a href="/wiki/Rhode_Island" title="Rhode Island">\n        Rhode Island\n       </a>\n       , with winds downing a tree and two electrical poles in the city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_Rhode_Island" title="Warwick, Rhode Island">\n        Warwick\n       </a>\n       . In\n       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">\n        Vermont\n       </a>\n       , 2.5\xc2\xa0in (64\xc2\xa0mm) of rain in\n       <a href="/wiki/Chittenden_County,_Vermont" title="Chittenden County, Vermont">\n        Chittenden County\n       </a>\n       caused cars to hydroplane on\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_89" title="Interstate 89">\n        Interstate 89\n       </a>\n       , resulting in many automobile accidents. The storm brought 3 to 5\xc2\xa0in (76 to 127\xc2\xa0mm) of precipitation to isolated areas of Maine and up to 9\xc2\xa0in (230\xc2\xa0mm) near\n       <a href="/wiki/Patten,_Maine" title="Patten, Maine">\n        Patten\n       </a>\n       . Several roads were inundated or washed out by overflowing brooks and streams, including sections of\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_1" title="U.S. Route 1">\n        U.S. Route 1\n       </a>\n       and Maine\n       <a href="/wiki/Maine_State_Route_11" title="Maine State Route 11">\n        routes 11\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maine_State_Route_159" title="Maine State Route 159">\n        159\n       </a>\n       . Several structures and one parked vehicle were also affected by the waters. Wind gusts up to 60\xc2\xa0mph (97\xc2\xa0km/h) also impacted parts of Maine, felling trees and causing power outages in\n       <a href="/wiki/Bar_Harbor,_Maine" title="Bar Harbor, Maine">\n        Bar Harbor\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bar_Harbor,_Maine" title="Bar Harbor, Maine">\n        Blue Hill\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Dover-Foxcroft,_Maine" title="Dover-Foxcroft, Maine">\n        Dover-Foxcroft\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Sedgwick,_Maine" title="Sedgwick, Maine">\n        Sedgwick Ridge\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sorrento,_Maine" title="Sorrento, Maine">\n        Sorrento\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In Canada, the remnants of Katrina brought rainfall amounts in excess of 3.94\xc2\xa0in (100\xc2\xa0mm) to many locations between the\n       <a href="/wiki/Niagara_Peninsula" title="Niagara Peninsula">\n        Niagara Peninsula\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">\n        Saint Lawrence River\n       </a>\n       valley.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Severe local flooding occurred in\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">\n        Quebec\n       </a>\n       , forcing the evacuations of dozens of homes in some communities as rivers began overflowing their banks and sewage systems were becoming overwhelmed by the influx of precipitation. Inundated and washed out roads, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Route_138" title="Quebec Route 138">\n        Route 138\n       </a>\n       along the north shore of the Saint Lawrence River,\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Route_172" title="Quebec Route 172">\n        Route 172\n       </a>\n       north of\n       <a href="/wiki/Tadoussac" title="Tadoussac">\n        Tadoussac\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Route_385" title="Quebec Route 385">\n        Route 385\n       </a>\n       near\n       <a href="/wiki/Forestville,_Quebec" title="Forestville, Quebec">\n        Forestville\n       </a>\n       left several communities isolated for at least a week.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">\n        Aftermath\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote         </a>\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            <span class="sortkey" style="display:none">\n             7010295200000000000\xe2\x99\xa0\n            </span>\n <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economic_effects_of_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Economic effects of Hurricane Katrina">\n        Economic effects of Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The economic effects of the storm reached high levels. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">\n        Bush Administration\n       </a>\n       sought $105 billion for repairs and reconstruction in the region,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which did not account for damage to the economy caused by potential interruption of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">\n        oil\n       </a>\n       supply, destruction of the Gulf Coast\'s highway infrastructure, and exports of commodities such as grain. Katrina damaged or destroyed 30\n       <a href="/wiki/Oil_platform" title="Oil platform">\n        oil platforms\n       </a>\n       and caused the closure of nine\n       <a href="/wiki/Oil_refinery" title="Oil refinery">\n        refineries\n       </a>\n       ;\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-katreport_48-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-katreport-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the total shut-in oil production from the Gulf of Mexico in the six-month period following Katrina was approximately 24% of the annual production and the shut-in gas production for the same period was about 18%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The forestry industry in Mississippi was also affected, as 1.3\xc2\xa0million acres (5,300\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of forest lands were destroyed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRS_environment_93-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CRS_environment-93">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The total loss to the forestry industry from Katrina is calculated to rise to about $5 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRS_environment_93-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CRS_environment-93">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Furthermore, hundreds of thousands of local residents were left unemployed. Before the hurricane, the region supported approximately one million non-farm jobs, with 600,000 of them in New Orleans. It is estimated that the total economic impact in Louisiana and Mississippi may eventually exceed $150 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Forensic accountants were involved in the assessment of economic damages resulting from this catastrophe.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Katrina displaced over one million people from the central Gulf coast to elsewhere across the United States, becoming the largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">\n        diaspora\n       </a>\n       in the history of the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">\n        Houston, Texas\n       </a>\n       , had an increase of 35,000 people;\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">\n        Mobile, Alabama\n       </a>\n       , gained over 24,000; Baton Rouge, Louisiana, over 15,000; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hammond,_Louisiana" title="Hammond, Louisiana">\n        Hammond, Louisiana\n       </a>\n       , received over 10,000, nearly doubling its size.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" title="Chicago, Illinois">\n        Chicago, Illinois\n       </a>\n       received over 6,000 people, the most of any non-southern city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By late January 2006, about 200,000 people were once again living in New Orleans, less than half of the pre-storm population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popestimate_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-popestimate-98">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By July 1, 2006, when new population estimates were calculated by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">\n        U.S. Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       , the state of Louisiana showed a population decline of 219,563, or 4.87%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popdecline_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-popdecline-99">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, some\n       <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">\n        insurance companies\n       </a>\n       have stopped insuring homeowners in the area because of the high costs from Hurricanes Katrina and Rita, or have raised homeowners\' insurance premiums to cover their risk.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_effects">\n        Environmental effects\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Murphy_Oil_USA_refinery_spill" title="Murphy Oil USA refinery spill">\n        Murphy Oil USA refinery spill\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="font-size:92%; float:right; margin-top:0; margin-left:10px; margin-right:0;">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="3" style="background:#ccf;">\n         <b>\n          Large oil spills caused by Hurricane Katrina\n         </b>\n         <br/>\n         <small>\n          Spills exceeding 10,000\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_gallon" title="US gallon">\n           US gallons\n          </a>\n          (38,000\n          <a href="/wiki/Litre" title="Litre">\n           L\n          </a>\n          )\n         </small>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msnbcspills_101-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-msnbcspills-101">\n           [100]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th rowspan="2">\n         Spill Location\n        </th>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Quantity\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n       Chevron (\n         <a href="/wiki/Empire,_Louisiana" title="Empire, Louisiana">\n          Empire\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;">\n         991,000\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;">\n         3,750,000\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Murphy Oil (\n         <a Chalmette\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;">\n         819,000\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:right;">\n         3,100,000\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bass Enterprises (\n         <a href="/wiki/Pointe_%C3%A0_la_Hache,_Louisiana" title="Pointe \xc3\xa0 la Hache, Louisiana">\n          Pointe
