width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BUSHKATRINA.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         President Bush stands with\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Defense" title="Secretary of Defense">\n          Secretary of Defense\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Donald_Rumsfeld" title="Donald Rumsfeld">\n          Donald Rumsfeld\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Labor" title="Secretary of Labor">\n          Secretary of Labor\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Elaine_Chao" title="Elaine Chao">\n          Elaine Chao\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="Secretary of Health and Human Services">\n          Secretary of Health and Human Services\n         </a>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mike_Leavitt" title="Mike Leavitt">\n          Mike Leavitt\n         </a>\n         during a press conference from the\n         <a href="/wiki/White_House_Rose_Garden" title="White House Rose Garden">\n          Rose Garden\n         </a>\n         , regarding the devastation along the Gulf Coast caused by Katrina.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Within the United States and as delineated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Response_Plan" title="National Response Plan">\n        National Response Plan\n       </a>\n       , disaster response and planning is first and foremost a local government responsibility. When local government exhausts its resources, it then requests specific additional resources from the county level. The request process proceeds similarly from the county to the state to the federal government as additional resource needs are identified. Many of the problems that arose developed from inadequate planning and back-up communication systems at various levels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgovwh_121-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-usgovwh-121">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some\n       <a href="/wiki/Disaster_recovery" title="Disaster recovery">\n        disaster recovery\n       </a>\n       response to Katrina began before the storm, with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency_of_the_United_States" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency of the United States">\n        Federal Emergency Management Agency\n       </a>\n       (FEMA) preparations that ranged from logistical supply deployments to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mortuary" title="Mortuary">\n        mortuary\n       </a>\n       team with refrigerated trucks. A network of volunteers began rendering assistance to local residents and residents emerging from New Orleans and surrounding parishes as soon as the storm made landfall (even though many were directed to not enter the area), and continued for more than six months after the storm\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgovwh_121-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-usgovwh-121">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Of the 60,000 people stranded in New Orleans, the Coast Guard rescued more than 33,500.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GAO-06-903_122-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GAO-06-903-122">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Congress recognized the Coast Guard\'s response with an official entry in the Congressional Record,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S._246_123-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-S._246-123">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_States" title="Military of the United States">\n        Armed Service\n       </a>\n       was awarded the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidential_Unit_Citation_(US)" title="Presidential Unit Citation (US)">\n        Presidential Unit Citation\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Northern_Command" title="United States Northern Command">\n        United States Northern Command\n       </a>\n       established\n       <a href="/wiki/Joint_Task_Force_Katrina" title="Joint Task Force Katrina">\n        Joint Task Force (JTF) Katrina\n       </a>\n       based out of\n       <a href="/wiki/Camp_Shelby" title="Camp Shelby">\n        Camp Shelby\n       </a>\n       , Mississippi, to act as the military\'s on-scene response on Sunday, August 28, with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Army" title="US Army">\n        US Army\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_general_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant general (United States)">\n        Lieutenant General\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Russel_L._Honor%C3%A9" title="Russel L. Honor\xc3\xa9">\n        Russel L. Honor\xc3\xa9\n       </a>\n       as commander.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Approximately 58,000 National Guard personnel were activated to deal with the storm\'s aftermath, with troops coming from all 50 states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       also activated volunteer members of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_Air_Patrol" title="Civil Air Patrol">\n        Civil Air Patrol\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Michael Chertoff,\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Secretary of Homeland Security">\n        Secretary\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security" title="United States Department of Homeland Security">\n        Department of Homeland Security\n       </a>\n       , decided to take over the federal, state, and local operations officially on August 30, 2005, citing the National Response Plan.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was refused by Governor Blanco who indicated that her National Guard could manage. Early in September, Congress authorized a total of $62.3 billion in aid for victims.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Additionally, President Bush enlisted the help of former presidents\n       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">\n        Bill Clinton\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">\n        George H. W. Bush\n       </a>\n       to raise additional voluntary contributions, much as they did after the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">\n        2004 Indian Ocean earthquake\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">\n        tsunami\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States" title="Flag of the United States">\n        American flags\n       </a>\n       were also ordered to be\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Half-staff" title="Half-staff">\n        half-staff\n       </a>\n       from September 2, 2005, to September 20, 2005, in honor of the victims.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       FEMA provided housing assistance (rental assistance,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FEMA_Trailer" title="FEMA Trailer">\n        trailers\n       </a>\n       , etc.) to more than 700,000 applicants\xe2\x80\x94families and individuals. However, only one-fifth of the trailers requested in Orleans Parish were supplied, resulting in an enormous housing shortage in the city of New Orleans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many local areas voted to not allow the trailers, and many areas had no utilities, a requirement prior to placing the trailers. To provide for additional housing, FEMA has also paid for the hotel costs of 12,000 individuals and families displaced by Katrina through February 7, 2006, when a final deadline was set for the end of hotel cost coverage. After this deadline, evacuees were still eligible to receive federal assistance, which could be used towards either apartment rent, additional hotel stays, or fixing their ruined homes, although FEMA no longer paid for hotels directly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As of March 30, 2010, there were still 260 families living in FEMA-provided trailers in Louisiana and Mississippi.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Law enforcement and public safety agencies, from across the United States, provided a "\n       <a href="/wiki/Mutual_aid_(emergency_services)" title="Mutual aid (emergency services)">\n        mutual aid\n       </a>\n       " response to Louisiana and New Orleans in the weeks following the disaster. Many agencies responded with manpower and equipment from as far away as\n       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">\n        California\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">\n        Michigan\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">\n        Nevada\n       </a>\n       , New York, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       . This response was welcomed by local Louisiana authorities as their staff were either becoming fatigued, stretched too thin, or even quitting from the job.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Two weeks after the storm, more than half of the states were involved in providing shelter for evacuees. By four weeks after the storm, evacuees had been registered in all 50 states and in 18,700 zip codes\xe2\x80\x94half of the nation\'s residential postal zones. Most evacuees had stayed within 250 miles (400\xc2\xa0km), but 240,000 households went to Houston and other cities over 250 miles (400\xc2\xa0km) away and another 60,000 households went over 750 miles (1,200\xc2\xa0km) away.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_of_government_response">\n        Criticism of government response\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of government response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        Criticism of government response to Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USNS_Comfort.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2100" data-file-width="1500" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/USNS_Comfort.jpg/170px-USNS_Comfort.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/USNS_Comfort.jpg/255px-USNS_Comfort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/USNS_Comfort.jpg/340px-USNS_Comfort.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USNS_Comfort.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USNS_Comfort" title="USNS Comfort">\n          USNS\n          <i>\n           Comfort\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         takes on supplies at\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayport,_Florida" title="Mayport, Florida">\n          Mayport, Florida\n         </a>\n         , en route to the Gulf Coast.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The criticisms of the government\'s response to Hurricane Katrina primarily consisted of criticism of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_incompetence" title="Administrative incompetence">\n        mismanagement\n       </a>\n       and lack of\n       <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">\n        leadership\n       </a>\n       in the relief efforts in response to the storm and its aftermath. More specifically, the criticism focused on the delayed response to the flooding of New Orleans, and the subsequent state of chaos in the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thevenot_72-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-thevenot-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">\n        neologism\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Katrina\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/-gate" title="-gate">\n         gate\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       was coined to refer to this controversy, and was a runner-up for "2005 word of the year."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Within days of Katrina\'s August 29 landfall, public debate arose about the local, state and federal governments\' role in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Preparations_for_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Preparations for Hurricane Katrina">\n        preparations\n       </a>\n       for and response to the hurricane. Criticism was initially prompted by televised images of visibly shaken and frustrated political leaders, and of residents who remained stranded by flood waters without\n       <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">\n        water\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Food" title="Food">\n        food\n       </a>\n       , or shelter. Deaths from\n       <a href="/wiki/Thirst" title="Thirst">\n        thirst\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(medical)" title="Fatigue (medical)">\n        exhaustion\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Violence" title="Violence">\n        violence\n       </a>\n       days after the storm had passed fueled the criticism, as did the dilemma of the evacuees at facilities such as the Louisiana Superdome and the New Orleans Civic Center. Some alleged that\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" title="Race (classification of human beings)">\n        race\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">\n        class\n       </a>\n       , and other factors could have contributed to delays in government response. For example, during\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/A_Concert_for_Hurricane_Relief" title="A Concert for Hurricane Relief">\n         A Concert for Hurricane Relief\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , a benefit concert for victims of the hurricane, rapper\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">\n        Kanye West\n       </a>\n       veered off script and harshly criticized the government\'s response to the crisis, stating that "George Bush doesn\'t care about\n       <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">\n        black people\n       </a>\n       ."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In accordance with federal law, President George W. Bush directed the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Homeland_Security" title="Secretary of Homeland Security">\n        Secretary of the Department of Homeland Security\n       </a>\n       , Michael Chertoff, to coordinate the Federal response. Chertoff designated\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Brown" title="Michael D. Brown">\n        Michael D. Brown\n       </a>\n       , head of the Federal Emergency Management Agency, as the Principal Federal Official to lead the deployment and coordination of all federal response resources and forces in the Gulf Coast region. However, the President and Secretary Chertoff initially came under harsh criticism for what some perceived as a lack of planning and coordination. Brown claimed that Governor Blanco resisted their efforts and was unhelpful. Governor Blanco and her staff disputed this.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Eight days later, Brown was recalled to Washington and Coast Guard Vice Admiral\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thad_W._Allen" title="Thad W. Allen">\n        Thad W. Allen\n       </a>\n       replaced him as chief of hurricane relief operations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Three days after the recall, Michael D. Brown resigned as director of FEMA in spite of having received recent praise from President Bush.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Politicians, activists, pundits, and journalists also directed criticism at the local and state governments headed by Mayor Nagin of New Orleans and Louisiana Governor Blanco. Nagin and Blanco were criticized for failing to implement New Orleans\' evacuation plan and for ordering residents to a shelter of last resort without any provisions for food, water, security, or sanitary conditions. Perhaps the most important criticism of Nagin was that he delayed his emergency evacuation order until 19 hours before landfall, which led to hundreds of deaths of people who could not find any way out of the city.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CongressInvestigation_11-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CongressInvestigation-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The destruction wrought by Hurricane Katrina raised other, more general public policy issues about\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">\n        emergency management\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">\n        environmental policy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">\n        poverty\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">\n        unemployment\n       </a>\n       . The discussion of both the immediate response and of the broader public policy issues may have affected\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections" title="Elections">\n        elections\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Legislation" title="Legislation">\n        legislation\n       </a>\n       enacted at various\n       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">\n        levels of government\n       </a>\n       . The storm\'s devastation also prompted a Congressional investigation, which found that FEMA and the Red Cross "did not have a logistics capacity sophisticated enough to fully support the massive number of Gulf coast victims." Additionally, it placed responsibility for the disaster on all three levels of government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CongressInvestigation_11-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CongressInvestigation-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An ABC News\n       <a href="/wiki/Opinion_poll" title="Opinion poll">\n        poll\n       </a>\n       conducted on September 2, 2005, showed more blame was being directed at state and local governments (75%) than at the Federal government (67%), with 44% blaming Bush\'s leadership directly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abcnewspoll_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-abcnewspoll-141">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A later\n       <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">\n        CNN\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USAToday" title="USAToday">\n        USAToday\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallup_poll" title="Gallup poll">\n        Gallup poll\n       </a>\n       showed that respondents disagreed widely on who was to blame for the problems in the city following the hurricane \xe2\x80\x94 13% said Bush, 18% said federal agencies, 25% blamed state or local officials and 38% said no one was to blame.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnnpoll_142-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cnnpoll-142">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A 2013 pool of Louisiana Republicans found more (29%) blamed Barack Obama for the poor federal response to the hurricane than George W. Bush (28%), despite the fact that Bush was actually president during the storm and Obama merely a junior senator.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPM_143-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TPM-143">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snopes_144-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-snopes-144">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="International_response">\n        International response\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/International_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="International response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        International response to Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_relief_transport.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1082" data-file-width="2100" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Canadian_relief_transport.jpg/220px-Canadian_relief_transport.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Canadian_relief_transport.jpg/330px-Canadian_relief_transport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Canadian_relief_transport.jpg/440px-Canadian_relief_transport.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canadian_relief_transport.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">\n          United States Navy\n         </a>\n         personnel unload\n         <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n          Canadian\n         </a>\n         relief supplies from a\n         <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">\n          Royal Canadian Air Force\n         </a>\n         transport aircraft in\n         <a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">\n          Pensacola, Florida\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Over seventy countries pledged monetary donations or other assistance.\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">\n        Cuba\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">\n        Venezuela\n       </a>\n       (both considered as hostile to US government interest) were the first countries to offer assistance, pledging over $1 million, several mobile hospitals, water treatment plants, canned food, bottled water, heating oil, 1,100 doctors and 26.4 metric tons of medicine, though this aid was rejected by the U.S. government.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n        <a href="#cite_note-148">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">\n        Kuwait\n       </a>\n       made the largest single pledge, $500 million; other large donations were made by\n       <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">\n        Qatar\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">\n        United Arab Emirates\n       </a>\n       (each $100 million),\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">\n        South Korea\n       </a>\n       ($30 million),\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australia\n       </a>\n       ($10 million),\n       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">\n        India\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">\n        China\n       </a>\n       (both $5 million),\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       ($2 million),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n        <a href="#cite_note-149">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">\n        Pakistan\n       </a>\n       ($1.5 million),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">\n        Norway\n       </a>\n       ($1.8 million),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">\n        Bangladesh\n       </a>\n       ($1 million).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       India sent tarps, blankets and hygiene kits. An\n       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">\n        Indian Air Force\n       </a>\n       IL-76 aircraft delivered 25 tonnes of relief supplies for the Hurricane Katrina victims at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock_Air_Force_Base" title="Little Rock Air Force Base">\n        Little Rock Air Force Base\n       </a>\n       , Arkansas, on September 13, 2005.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">\n        Israel\n       </a>\n       sent an\n       <a href="/wiki/Israel_Defense_Forces" title="Israel Defense Forces">\n        IDF\n       </a>\n       delegation to New Orleans to transport aid equipment including 80 tons of food, disposable diapers, beds, blankets, generators and additional equipment which were donated from different governmental institutions, civilian institutions and the IDF.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Bush Administration announced in mid-September that it did not need Israeli divers and physicians to come to the United States for search and rescue missions, but a small team landed in New Orleans on September 10 to give assistance to operations already under way. The team administered first aid to survivors, rescued\n       <a href="/wiki/Abandoned_pets" title="Abandoned pets">\n        abandoned pets\n       </a>\n       and discovered hurricane victims.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Countries like\n       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">\n        Sri Lanka\n       </a>\n       , which was still recovering from the\n       <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake_and_tsunami" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake and tsunami">\n        Indian Ocean Tsunami\n       </a>\n       , also offered to help. Countries including\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Canadian response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Mexican response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        Mexico\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Singaporean_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Singaporean response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        Singapore\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       sent supplies, relief personnel (like\n       <a href="/wiki/Technisches_Hilfswerk" title="Technisches Hilfswerk">\n        Technisches Hilfswerk\n       </a>\n       ), troops, ships and water pumps to aid in the disaster recovery.\n       <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">\n        Belgium\n       </a>\n       sent in a team of relief personnel.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK" title="UK">\n        Britain\n       </a>\n       \'s donation of 350,000 emergency meals did not reach victims because of laws regarding\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mad_cow_disease" title="Mad cow disease">\n        mad cow disease\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Russian response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        initial offer\n       </a>\n       of two jets was declined by the U.S. State Department but accepted later. The\n       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">\n        French\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="French response to Hurricane Katrina">\n        offer\n       </a>\n       was also declined and requested later.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-governmental_organization_response">\n        Non-governmental organization response\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1803" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_15322_-_Photograph_by_Andrea_Booher_taken_on_09-05-2005_in_Texas.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Residents of Louisiana, who had to flee their homes because of Hurricane Katrina, are inside the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston_Astrodome" title="Houston Astrodome">\n          Houston Astrodome\n         </a>\n         and being helped by the Red Cross and other agencies and associations.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Red_Cross" title="American Red Cross">\n        American Red Cross\n       </a>\n       , America\'s Second Harvest (now known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Feeding_America" title="Feeding America">\n        Feeding America\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">\n        Southern Baptist Convention\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salvation_Army" title="Salvation Army">\n        Salvation Army\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">\n        Oxfam\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_Ground_Collective" title="Common Ground Collective">\n        Common Ground Collective\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Burners_Without_Borders" title="Burners Without Borders">\n        Burners Without Borders\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sfbg_157-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sfbg-157">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Communities" title="Emergency Communities">\n        Emergency Communities\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Habitat_for_Humanity" title="Habitat for Humanity">\n        Habitat for Humanity\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Charities" title="Catholic Charities">\n        Catholic Charities\n       </a>\n       , Service International, "A River of Hope",\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">\n        The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and many other charitable organizations provided help to the victims of the storm. They were not allowed into New Orleans proper by the National Guard for several days after the storm because of safety concerns. These organizations raised US$4.25 billion in donations by the public, with the Red Cross receiving over half of the donations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charity_Navigator_report_161-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Charity_Navigator_report-161">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some smaller organizations and individuals ignored the access restrictions and provided early relief. For example, two privately chartered planes from\n       <a href="/wiki/FasterCures" title="FasterCures">\n        FasterCures\n       </a>\n       evacuated 200 patents from Charity Hospital in New Orleans.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Volunteers from\n       <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">\n        amateur radio\n       </a>\n       \'s emergency service wing, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Amateur_Radio_Emergency_Service" title="Amateur Radio Emergency Service">\n        Amateur Radio Emergency Service\n       </a>\n       , provided communications in areas where the communications infrastructure had been damaged or totally destroyed, relaying everything from 911 traffic to messages home.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Hancock County, Mississippi, ham radio operators provided the only communications into or out of the area, and even served as 911 dispatchers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Many corporations also contributed to relief efforts. On September 13, 2005, it was reported that corporate donations to the relief effort were $409 million, and were expected to exceed $1 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">\n        <a href="#cite_note-165">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During and after the Hurricanes Katrina, Wilma and Rita, the American Red Cross had opened 1,470 shelters and registered 3.8 million overnight stays. None were allowed in New Orleans however. A total of 244,000 Red Cross workers (95% of which were non-paid volunteers) were utilized throughout these three hurricanes. In addition, 346,980 comfort kits (such as toothpaste, soap, washcloths and toys for children) and 205,360 cleanup kits (containing brooms, mops and bleach) were distributed. For mass care, the organization served 68 million snacks and meals to victims of the disasters and to rescue workers. The Red Cross also had its Disaster Health services meet 596,810 contacts, and Disaster Mental Health services met 826,590 contacts. Red Cross emergency financial assistance was provided to 1.4 million families. Hurricane Katrina was the first natural disaster in the United States in which the American Red Cross utilized its "Safe and Well" family location website.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARC_1_yr_166-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ARC_1_yr-166">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARC_2005AHS_facts_167-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ARC_2005AHS_facts-167">\n         [166]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the year following Katrina\'s strike on the Gulf Coast, The Salvation Army allocated donations of more than $365 million to serve more than 1.7 million people in nearly every state. The organization\'s immediate response to Hurricane Katrina included more than 5.7 million hot meals and about 8.3 million sandwiches, snacks, and drinks served in and around New Orleans. Its SATERN network of amateur radio operators picked up where modern communications left off to help locate more than 25,000 survivors. Salvation Army pastoral care counselors were on hand to comfort the emotional and spiritual needs of 277,000 individuals. As part of the overall effort, Salvation Army officers, employees, and volunteers contributed more than 900,000 hours of service.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Salvation_Army_168-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Salvation_Army-168">\n         [167]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis_of_New_Orleans_levee_failures">\n        Analysis of New Orleans levee failures\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/2005_levee_failures_in_Greater_New_Orleans" title="2005 levee failures in Greater New Orleans">\n        2005 levee failures in Greater New Orleans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg/170px-Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg/255px-Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg/340px-Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Katrina_Eye_viewed_from_Hurricane_Hunter.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of the eyewall of Hurricane Katrina taken on August 28, 2005, as seen from a\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">\n          NOAA\n         </a>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WP-3D_Orion" title="WP-3D Orion">\n          WP-3D\n         </a>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_hunter" title="Hurricane hunter">\n          hurricane hunter\n         </a>\n         aircraft before the storm made landfall on the United States\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" title="Gulf Coast">\n          Gulf Coast\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On April 5, 2006, months after independent investigators had demonstrated that levee failures were not caused by natural forces beyond intended design strength, Lieutenant General\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_Strock" title="Carl Strock">\n        Carl Strock\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_of_Engineers" title="Chief of Engineers">\n        Chief of Engineers\n       </a>\n       and Commander of the Corps of Engineers, testified before the United States Senate Subcommittee on Energy and Water that "We have now concluded we had problems with the design of the structure."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169">\n        <a href="#cite_note-169">\n         [168]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A June 2007 report released by the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Society_of_Civil_Engineers" title="American Society of Civil Engineers">\n        American Society of Civil Engineers\n       </a>\n       determined that the failures of the levees and floodwalls in New Orleans were found to be primarily the result of system design and construction flaws.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASCE_HKERP_report_47-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ASCE_HKERP_report-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="US Army Corps of Engineers">\n        US Army Corps of Engineers\n       </a>\n       is federally mandated in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1965" title="Flood Control Act of 1965">\n        Flood Control Act of 1965\n       </a>\n       with responsibility for the conception, design and construction of the region\'s flood-control system. According to report published in August 2015 in the official journal of the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Water_Council" title="World Water Council">\n        World Water Council\n       </a>\n       , the corps misinterpreted the results of a 1985 study and wrongly concluded that sheet piles in the flood walls needed to be driven to depths of only 17 feet (5\xc2\xa0m) instead of between 31 and 46 feet (9 and 14\xc2\xa0m). That decision saved approximately US$100 million, but significantly reduced overall engineering reliability.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170">\n        <a href="#cite_note-170">\n         [169]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other factors may have contributed to the flooding. According to the authors of Catastrophe in the Making (Island Press, 2009), the straight design and lack of outward flow into the Gulf allowed the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippi_River-Gulf_Outlet_Canal" title="Mississippi River-Gulf Outlet Canal">\n        Mississippi River-Gulf Outlet Canal\n       </a>\n       to become "the perfect shortcut for salt-water intrusion" which damaged buffering cypress forests and wetlands which historically had protected New Orleans from storm surge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171">\n        <a href="#cite_note-171">\n         [170]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Army Corps of Engineers built and maintained the canal. Furthermore, according to storm surge researcher Hassan Mashriqui:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        "Storm surge pushing across shallow Lake Borgne from the east is constrained by these MRGO levees to the south and, to the north, by the long-standing levees of the Intracoastal Waterway (GIWW). Initially ten or more miles apart, these two channels meet, and when they do, the water building between their levees is squeezed into a single channel \xe2\x80\x93 the Funnel \xe2\x80\x93 only 260 yards wide, constrained by levees 14 feet to 16 feet high\xe2\x80\xa6.In concert with the denuded marshes, it could increase the local storm surge hitting the Intracoastal Waterway by 20 percent to 40 percent \xe2\x80\x93 a critical and fundamental flaw."\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172">\n         <a href="#cite_note-172">\n          [171]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </p>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       The Corps of Engineers disputes these causalities.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173">\n        <a href="#cite_note-173">\n         [172]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Nonetheless, in June 2008, the Army Corps of Engineers New Orleans District submitted a Deep-Draft De-authorization Study of the MRGO which stated that "an economic evaluation of channel navigation use does not demonstrate a Federal interest in continued operation and maintenance of the channel." Congress ordered the MRGO closed as a direct result.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Many of the levees have been reconstructed since the time of Katrina. In reconstructing them, precautions were taken to bring the levees up to modern building code standards and to ensure their safety. For example, in every situation possible, the Corps of Engineers replaced I-walls with T-walls. T-walls have a horizontal concrete base that protects against soil erosion underneath the floodwalls.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Walls_174-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Walls-174">\n         [173]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, there are funding battles over the remaining levee improvements. In February 2008, the Bush administration requested that the state of Louisiana pay about $1.5 billion of an estimated $7.2 billion for Corps of Engineers levee work (in accordance with the principles of local cost sharing required by Congress as early as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Flood_Control_Act_of_1928" title="Flood Control Act of 1928">\n        Flood Control Act of 1928\n       </a>\n       ), a proposal which angered many Louisiana leaders.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-funding_175-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-funding-175">\n         [174]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On May 2, 2008, Louisiana Gov.\n       <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Jindal" title="Bobby Jindal">\n        Bobby Jindal\n       </a>\n       used a speech to The National Press Club to request that President Bush free up money to complete work on Louisiana\'s levees. Bush promised to include the levee funding in his 2009 budget, but rejected the idea of including the funding in a war bill, which would pass sooner.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BushJindal_176-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BushJindal-176">\n         [175]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media_involvement">\n        Media involvement\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Media_coverage_of_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Media coverage of Hurricane Katrina">\n        Media coverage of Hurricane Katrina\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Many representatives of the\n       <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">\n        news media\n       </a>\n       reporting on the aftermath of Hurricane Katrina became directly involved in the unfolding events, instead of simply reporting. Because of the loss of most means of communication, such as land-based and cellular telephone systems, field reporters in many cases became conduits for information between victims and authorities. The authorities, who monitored local and network news broadcasts, as well as internet sites, would then attempt to coordinate rescue efforts based on the reports. One illustration was when\n       <a href="/wiki/Geraldo_Rivera" title="Geraldo Rivera">\n        Geraldo Rivera\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">\n        Fox News\n       </a>\n       tearfully pleaded for authorities to either send help or evacuate the thousands of evacuees stranded at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ernest_N._Morial_Convention_Center" title="Ernest N. Morial Convention Center">\n        Ernest N. Morial Convention Center\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177">\n        <a href="#cite_note-177">\n         [176]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The role of AM radio was also of importance to the hundreds of thousands of persons with no other ties to news, providing emergency information regarding access to assistance for hurricane victims. Immediately after Katrina,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWL-AM" title="WWL-AM">\n        WWL-AM\n       </a>\n       was one of the few area radio stations in the area remaining on the air. This emergency service, simulcasted on shortwave outlet\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHRI" title="WHRI">\n        WHRI\n       </a>\n       , was named "\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Radio_Broadcasters_of_New_Orleans" title="United Radio Broadcasters of New Orleans">\n        The United Radio Broadcasters of New Orleans\n       </a>\n       ." Their ongoing nighttime broadcasts continued to be available up to 500\xc2\xa0mi (800\xc2\xa0km) away. Announcers continued to broadcast from improvised studio facilities after the storm damaged their main studios.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178">\n        <a href="#cite_note-178">\n         [177]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cellular_phone" title="Cellular phone">\n        cellular phone\n       </a>\n       antenna network was severely damaged and completely inoperable for several months.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The storm also brought a dramatic rise in the role of\n       <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">\n        Internet sites\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94especially\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blogging" title="Blogging">\n        blogging\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Community_journalism" title="Community journalism">\n        community journalism\n       </a>\n       . One example was the effort of\n       <i>\n        NOLA.com\n       </i>\n       , the web affiliate of New Orleans\'\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Times-Picayune" title="The Times-Picayune">\n         Times-Picayune\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . A group of reporters were awarded the Breaking News\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">\n        Pulitzer Prize\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_BN_179-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer_BN-179">\n         [178]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and shared the Public Service Pulitzer with the Biloxi-based\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sun_Herald" title="The Sun Herald">\n         Sun Herald\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_PS_180-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer_PS-180">\n         [179]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The newspaper\'s coverage was carried for days only on NOLA\'s blogs, as the newspaper lost its presses and evacuated its building as water rose around it on August 30. The site became an international focal point for news by local media, and also became a vital link for rescue operations and later for reuniting scattered residents, as it accepted and posted thousands of individual pleas for rescue on its blogs and forums. NOLA was monitored constantly by an array of rescue teams\xe2\x80\x94from individuals to the Coast Guard\xe2\x80\x94which used information in rescue efforts. Much of this information was relayed from trapped victims via the SMS functions of their cell phones, to friends and relatives outside the area, who then relayed the information back to NOLA.com. The aggregation of community journalism, user photos and the use of the internet site as a collaborative response to the storm attracted international attention, and was called a watershed moment in journalism.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OJR_NOLA_181-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OJR_NOLA-181">\n         [180]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the wake of these online-only efforts, the Pulitzer Committee for the first time opened all its categories to online entries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pulitzer_speech_182-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pulitzer_speech-182">\n         [181]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As the U.S. military and rescue services regained control over the city, there were restrictions on the activity of the media. On September 9, the military leader of the relief effort announced that reporters would have "zero access" to efforts to recover bodies in New Orleans. Immediately following this announcement, CNN filed a\n       <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">\n        lawsuit\n       </a>\n       and obtained a temporary\n       <a href="/wiki/Restraining_order" title="Restraining order">\n        restraining order\n       </a>\n       against the ban. The next day the government backed down and reversed the ban.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Media_Ban_183-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Media_Ban-183">\n         [182]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">\n        Retirement\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Atlantic_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Atlantic hurricane names">\n        List of retired Atlantic hurricane names\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Because of the large death toll and destruction of property along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast" title="Gulf Coast">\n        Gulf Coast\n       </a>\n       , the name Katrina was officially retired on April 6, 2006, by the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">\n        World Meteorological Organization\n       </a>\n       at the request of the U.S. government. The name will never again be used for another\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_hurricane" title="North Atlantic hurricane">\n        North Atlantic hurricane\n       </a>\n       . It was replaced by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katia" title="Hurricane Katia">\n        Katia\n       </a>\n       on List III of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_naming_lists" title="Atlantic hurricane naming lists">\n        Atlantic hurricane naming lists\n       </a>\n       , which was used in the\n       <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2011 Atlantic hurricane season">\n        2011 Atlantic hurricane season\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184">\n        <a href="#cite_note-184">\n         [183]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Studies_concerning_post-Katrina_victims">\n        Studies concerning post-Katrina victims\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       An article published in the\n       <i>\n        Community Mental Health Journal\n       </i>\n       from January 2016 revealed information about a recent study on the psychosocial needs of Hurricane Katrina evacuees that temporarily resided in Dallas, Texas. More than one-fourth of the sample met the criteria for major depressive disorder (MDD). About one-third of the individuals received a referral to mental health services for meeting symptom criteria for incident MDD and PTSD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185">\n        <a href="#cite_note-185">\n         [184]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In a study published in\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Maternal_and_Child_Health_Journal" title="Maternal and Child Health Journal">\n         Maternal and Child Health Journal\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , five-to seven years after the disaster, 308 New Orleans pregnant women were interviewed about their exposure to Katrina. Researchers found that there were associations between experiencing damage during Katrina and birthweight, thus researchers concluded that natural disasters may have long-term effects on pregnancy outcomes. Furthermore, it was concluded that women who are most vulnerable to disaster may be more vulnerable to poor pregnancy outcome.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186">\n        <a href="#cite_note-186">\n         [185]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       From a September 2015 journal of\n       <i>\n        Current Psychology\n       </i>\n       , a study examined the attitudes of older, long-term residents of Baton Rouge, Louisiana toward displaced newcomers to their community. After using multiple tests, analyses, and descriptive statistics, the study suggested residents grew to become more patient, tolerant, and friendly towards newcomers. The study also suggests, however, that residents felt more fearful and suspicious of the evacuees, as well as the fact that they were being taken advantage of more.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187">\n        <a href="#cite_note-187">\n         [186]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reconstruction">\n        Reconstruction\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_of_New_Orleans" title="Reconstruction of New Orleans">\n        Reconstruction of New Orleans\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg/220px-FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg/330px-FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg/440px-FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FEMA_-_21590_-_Photograph_by_Marvin_Nauman_taken_on_01-21-2006_in_Louisiana.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Volunteers from\n         <a href="/wiki/AmeriCorps" title="AmeriCorps">\n          AmeriCorps\n         </a>\n         in New Orleans, January 2006\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Reconstruction of each section of the southern portion of Louisiana has been addressed in the Army Corps LACPR (Louisiana Coastal Protection and Restoration) Final Technical Report, which identifies areas to not be rebuilt and areas where buildings need to be elevated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_LACPR_Home_Page_188-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-The_LACPR_Home_Page-188">\n         [187]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Technical Report includes:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        locations of possible new levees to be built\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        suggested existing levee modifications\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        "Inundation Zones", "Water depths less than 14 feet, Raise-In-Place of Structures", "Water depths greater than 14 feet, Buyout of Structures", "Velocity Zones" and "Buyout of Structures" areas for five different scenarios.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. Army Corps of Engineers submitted the report to the U.S. Congress for consideration, planning, and response in mid-2009.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n
